Time as a Flowing Container
Razi establishes that time is a flowing container (ẓarf) by analyzing everyday speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that time is a container (ẓarf) for events and that it must be flowing, not permanent.

Core Idea
Time is the flowing container that holds events, not a fixed object.

Razi begins his proof by examining ordinary language. When we say 'I will come when the sun rises,' we imply a specific time that serves as a container for both the coming and the rising. Razi then argues that this time cannot be a static, permanent entity because we await it as future. Instead, it must be something flowing and passing away.

Guided Path
1
Analyze the phrase
Notice how Razi extracts the concept of a specific time from the common expression 'I will come when the sun rises.' He shows that this implies a single time acting as a container.
2
Identify the two possibilities
Razi presents a dichotomy: the time in question is either permanent (bāqin thābit) or flowing (sayyāl). Understand each option.
3
Reject permanence
If time were permanent, it would be present now, but we perceive it as future and awaited. Badīhat al-ʿaql (sound reason) confirms that it is not present, so it must be flowing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا عرفت هذا فلنبحث عن معنى قولهم : أتيك إذا طلعت الشمس فإنه لا معنى لهذا الكلام إلا أن القائل يقول : آتيك في الوقت الذي تطلع فيه الشمس ، وهذا تصريح بإثبات وقت واحد بعينه يحصل فيه مجيء هذا القائل ، ويحصل فيه طلوع الشمس . فنقول : ذلك الوقت الذي حكمت الفطرة السليمة بجعله ظرفاً لهذا المجيء ، ولطلوع الشمس . إما أن يكون شيئاً باقياً ثابتاً، أو شيئاً سيالاً منقضياً ، والأول باطل ، وإلا لكان حاصلا في الحال، فوجب أن لا يكون منتظراً ولا مستقبلاً . وبديهة العقل حاكمة بأن ذلك الوقت غير حاضر في الحال بل هو منتظر الوجود. فثبت أنه أمر سيال . ثم ذلك السيال إما أن يكون شيئاً من جنس حركات الأفلاك والكواكب ، أو صفة من صفاتها ، أو يكون موجوداً مغايراً لهذين القسمين . والأول باطل ، لأن ذلك الوقت شيء حكمت الفطرة السليمة بكونه ظرفاً للحركة الفلكية ، وظرف الحركة الفلكية لا يكون نفس الحركة الفلكية، فإنه لما قال: أتيك إذا طلعت الشمس ، فمعناه : أتيك في الوقت الذي يكون ظرفاً لطلوع الشمس . وأما القسم الثاني : وهو أن يكون ذلك الشيء صفة من صفات الحركة الفلكية ، فهو أظهر فساداً ، لأن ذلك الشيء ظرف للحركة الفلكية ، والحركة الفلكية جارية مجرى الظرف بجميع صفاتها ونعوتها ، فلو كان الظرف شيئاً من صفات تلك الحركة ، لزم كون الشيء الواحد بالنسبة إلى الشيء الواحد ظرفاً له ومظروفاً له. وهو محال . وأيضاً : فلو قال قائل: إنه تعالى يفعل الفعل الفلاني عند وقوف الأفلاك والكواكب عن حركاتها ، لم يكن هذا الكلام كلاماً معلوم الفساد والبطلان في بديهة العقل . فلو كان هذا الظرف شيئاً من الحركات الفلكية أو شيئاً من أحوال تلك الحركات. لكان هذا الكلام مقطوع الفساد في بديهة العقل . لأن حصول الحادث لا في وقت معين : معلوم الامتناع في البديهة . وأيضاً : فلا حال من أحوال الحركة الفلكية ، ولا صفة من صفاتها إلا وصريح العقل يحكم بأنها وقعت في الوقت الفلاني . في الماضي ، أو سيقع في الوقت الفلاني في المستقبل . فثبت بما ذكرنا : أن ذلك الظرف ليس هو الحركة الفلكية ، ولا صفة من صفاتها . فثبت : وجود موجود سیال ، ليس هو الحركة الفلكية ولا صفة من صفاتها . وذلك هو الزمان
If you have understood this, let us investigate the meaning of their statement: 'I will come to you when the sun rises.' For there is no meaning to this statement except that the speaker says: 'I will come to you at the time when the sun rises.' And this is an explicit assertion of a single specific time in which this speaker's coming occurs and in which the sun's rising occurs. We say: That time which sound nature judged to be a container (ẓarf) for this coming and for the sun's rising — either it is something permanent (bāqin thābit) or something flowing (sayyālan) and passing away (munqaḍin). The first is false, for otherwise it would be present now, so it would necessarily not be awaited nor future. And sound reason (badīhat al-ʿaql) judges that that time is not present now but rather is awaited in existence. So it is established that it is a flowing thing. Then that flowing thing is either something from the class of the movements of the celestial spheres and planets, or an attribute (ṣifa) of them, or an existence that is other than these two divisions. The first is false, because that time is something that sound nature judged to be a container for the celestial movement, and the container of the celestial movement cannot be the celestial movement itself. For when he said: 'I will come to you when the sun rises,' its meaning is: 'I will come to you at the time that is a container for the sun's rising.' As for the second division — that it is an attribute of the celestial movement — it is even more clearly corrupt, because that thing is a container for the celestial movement, and the celestial movement functions as a container with all its attributes and descriptions. So if the container were something from the attributes of that movement, it would entail that a single thing, with respect to a single thing, is both a container (ẓarf) for it and contained (maẓrūf) in it, which is impossible. Also, if someone were to say: 'God Most High does such and such act at the cessation of the celestial spheres and planets from their movements,' this statement would not be known to be corrupt and invalid in the immediate intuition (badīha) of the mind. So if this container were something from the celestial movements or something from the states of those movements, this statement would be certainly corrupt in the immediate intuition of the mind, because the occurrence of an event at no specific time is known to be impossible in immediate intuition. Also, there is no state (ḥāl) from the states of the celestial movement, nor any attribute from its attributes, except that clear reason judges that it occurred at such and such time in the past or will occur at such and such time in the future. So it is established, by what we have mentioned, that that container is not the celestial movement nor an attribute of its attributes. So it is established: the existence of a flowing existent (mawjūd sayyāl) that is not the celestial movement nor an attribute of its attributes. And that is time (al-zamān).
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage contains a rational proof for the existence of time (zaman) as a distinct flowing entity. The author starts by analyzing the common statement 'I will come to you when the sun rises,' which he interprets as an assertion of a specific time that serves as a container (zarf) for both the coming and the rising. He then examines the nature of this time. First, he argues that it cannot be a permanent, fixed thing because then it would be present now, but we perceive it as future and awaited; hence it must be flowing (sayyal) and passing away. Next, he considers whether this flowing thing is the celestial movement itself, an attribute of that movement, or something else. He rejects the first possibility by noting that the time is a container for the movement, but the container cannot be identical to the movement it contains; the phrase 'I will come to you when the sun rises' means 'I will come to you at the time that is a container for the sun's rising,' so the time is distinct from the rising. He then rejects the second possibility (that it is an attribute of the movement) with a stronger argument: if the container were an attribute of the movement, then the movement itself would be functioning as a container for its own attribute, leading to the absurdity that one thing is both container and contained relative to the same thing. He provides additional supporting arguments: if someone says 'God does an act when the planets stop moving,' that statement is not obviously false to intuition, but if the 'when' (the container) were the movement itself or its attribute, then the statement 'at cessation of movement' would be self-contradictory because at that moment there is no movement to serve as the container. Furthermore, every attribute or state of celestial motion is itself located in some time, so the time cannot be one of those attributes. Finally, he concludes that the container (time) is neither the celestial movement nor its attributes, establishing the existence of a flowing entity that is distinct from them, and that entity is time (al-zaman).

Key Terms
زمان
سيال
ظرف
فطرة
بديهة العقل

D) Because it would have no attributes.

Key Takeaway
Time is the flowing container of events, not a fixed entity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

You say you will repent 'when' — but when is a flowing container that never stays. Are you waiting for a permanent 'when' that doesn't exist? What is stopping you from turning to Allah right now, in this very flowing moment?

Time is Not Celestial Motion
Razi refutes that time is the celestial movement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why time cannot be identical to the movement of celestial spheres or planets.

Core Idea
The container of motion cannot be the motion itself.

Having established that time is flowing, Razi now considers whether it could be the celestial movement itself. He argues that since time is a container (ẓarf) for that movement, it cannot be identical to what it contains. Just as the phrase 'when the sun rises' means 'at the time that contains the rising,' the time is distinct from the rising.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three candidates
Razi lists three possibilities for the flowing entity: celestial motion, an attribute of that motion, or something else.
2
Focus on the first candidate
He rejects that time is the celestial motion itself because time is a container for motion, and a container cannot be identical to its content.
This uses the example 'when the sun rises'.
3
Understand the argument
If time were the movement, then 'I will come when the sun rises' would mean 'I will come at the sun's rising' (i.e., at the movement itself), but the correct interpretation is 'I will come at the time that contains the rising.' Distinguish between container and contained.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إذا عرفت هذا فلنبحث عن معنى قولهم : أتيك إذا طلعت الشمس فإنه لا معنى لهذا الكلام إلا أن القائل يقول : آتيك في الوقت الذي تطلع فيه الشمس ، وهذا تصريح بإثبات وقت واحد بعينه يحصل فيه مجيء هذا القائل ، ويحصل فيه طلوع الشمس . فنقول : ذلك الوقت الذي حكمت الفطرة السليمة بجعله ظرفاً لهذا المجيء ، ولطلوع الشمس . إما أن يكون شيئاً باقياً ثابتاً، أو شيئاً سيالاً منقضياً ، والأول باطل ، وإلا لكان حاصلا في الحال، فوجب أن لا يكون منتظراً ولا مستقبلاً . وبديهة العقل حاكمة بأن ذلك الوقت غير حاضر في الحال بل هو منتظر الوجود. فثبت أنه أمر سيال . ثم ذلك السيال إما أن يكون شيئاً من جنس حركات الأفلاك والكواكب ، أو صفة من صفاتها ، أو يكون موجوداً مغايراً لهذين القسمين . والأول باطل ، لأن ذلك الوقت شيء حكمت الفطرة السليمة بكونه ظرفاً للحركة الفلكية ، وظرف الحركة الفلكية لا يكون نفس الحركة الفلكية، فإنه لما قال: أتيك إذا طلعت الشمس ، فمعناه : أتيك في الوقت الذي يكون ظرفاً لطلوع الشمس . وأما القسم الثاني : وهو أن يكون ذلك الشيء صفة من صفات الحركة الفلكية ، فهو أظهر فساداً ، لأن ذلك الشيء ظرف للحركة الفلكية ، والحركة الفلكية جارية مجرى الظرف بجميع صفاتها ونعوتها ، فلو كان الظرف شيئاً من صفات تلك الحركة ، لزم كون الشيء الواحد بالنسبة إلى الشيء الواحد ظرفاً له ومظروفاً له. وهو محال . وأيضاً : فلو قال قائل: إنه تعالى يفعل الفعل الفلاني عند وقوف الأفلاك والكواكب عن حركاتها ، لم يكن هذا الكلام كلاماً معلوم الفساد والبطلان في بديهة العقل . فلو كان هذا الظرف شيئاً من الحركات الفلكية أو شيئاً من أحوال تلك الحركات. لكان هذا الكلام مقطوع الفساد في بديهة العقل . لأن حصول الحادث لا في وقت معين : معلوم الامتناع في البديهة . وأيضاً : فلا حال من أحوال الحركة الفلكية ، ولا صفة من صفاتها إلا وصريح العقل يحكم بأنها وقعت في الوقت الفلاني . في الماضي ، أو سيقع في الوقت الفلاني في المستقبل . فثبت بما ذكرنا : أن ذلك الظرف ليس هو الحركة الفلكية ، ولا صفة من صفاتها . فثبت : وجود موجود سیال ، ليس هو الحركة الفلكية ولا صفة من صفاتها . وذلك هو الزمان
If you have understood this, let us investigate the meaning of their statement: 'I will come to you when the sun rises.' For there is no meaning to this statement except that the speaker says: 'I will come to you at the time when the sun rises.' And this is an explicit assertion of a single specific time in which this speaker's coming occurs and in which the sun's rising occurs. We say: That time which sound nature judged to be a container (ẓarf) for this coming and for the sun's rising — either it is something permanent (bāqin thābit) or something flowing (sayyālan) and passing away (munqaḍin). The first is false, for otherwise it would be present now, so it would necessarily not be awaited nor future. And sound reason (badīhat al-ʿaql) judges that that time is not present now but rather is awaited in existence. So it is established that it is a flowing thing. Then that flowing thing is either something from the class of the movements of the celestial spheres and planets, or an attribute (ṣifa) of them, or an existence that is other than these two divisions. The first is false, because that time is something that sound nature judged to be a container for the celestial movement, and the container of the celestial movement cannot be the celestial movement itself. For when he said: 'I will come to you when the sun rises,' its meaning is: 'I will come to you at the time that is a container for the sun's rising.' As for the second division — that it is an attribute of the celestial movement — it is even more clearly corrupt, because that thing is a container for the celestial movement, and the celestial movement functions as a container with all its attributes and descriptions. So if the container were something from the attributes of that movement, it would entail that a single thing, with respect to a single thing, is both a container (ẓarf) for it and contained (maẓrūf) in it, which is impossible. Also, if someone were to say: 'God Most High does such and such act at the cessation of the celestial spheres and planets from their movements,' this statement would not be known to be corrupt and invalid in the immediate intuition (badīha) of the mind. So if this container were something from the celestial movements or something from the states of those movements, this statement would be certainly corrupt in the immediate intuition of the mind, because the occurrence of an event at no specific time is known to be impossible in immediate intuition. Also, there is no state (ḥāl) from the states of the celestial movement, nor any attribute from its attributes, except that clear reason judges that it occurred at such and such time in the past or will occur at such and such time in the future. So it is established, by what we have mentioned, that that container is not the celestial movement nor an attribute of its attributes. So it is established: the existence of a flowing existent (mawjūd sayyāl) that is not the celestial movement nor an attribute of its attributes. And that is time (al-zamān).
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage contains a rational proof for the existence of time (zaman) as a distinct flowing entity. The author starts by analyzing the common statement 'I will come to you when the sun rises,' which he interprets as an assertion of a specific time that serves as a container (zarf) for both the coming and the rising. He then examines the nature of this time. First, he argues that it cannot be a permanent, fixed thing because then it would be present now, but we perceive it as future and awaited; hence it must be flowing (sayyal) and passing away. Next, he considers whether this flowing thing is the celestial movement itself, an attribute of that movement, or something else. He rejects the first possibility by noting that the time is a container for the movement, but the container cannot be identical to the movement it contains; the phrase 'I will come to you when the sun rises' means 'I will come to you at the time that is a container for the sun's rising,' so the time is distinct from the rising. He then rejects the second possibility (that it is an attribute of the movement) with a stronger argument: if the container were an attribute of the movement, then the movement itself would be functioning as a container for its own attribute, leading to the absurdity that one thing is both container and contained relative to the same thing. He provides additional supporting arguments: if someone says 'God does an act when the planets stop moving,' that statement is not obviously false to intuition, but if the 'when' (the container) were the movement itself or its attribute, then the statement 'at cessation of movement' would be self-contradictory because at that moment there is no movement to serve as the container. Furthermore, every attribute or state of celestial motion is itself located in some time, so the time cannot be one of those attributes. Finally, he concludes that the container (time) is neither the celestial movement nor its attributes, establishing the existence of a flowing entity that is distinct from them, and that entity is time (al-zaman).

ظرف
مظروف

Checkpoint
Why does Razi reject that time is the celestial movement itself?
A) Because celestial movements are not flowing.
B) Because time is a container and the container cannot be its own content.
C) Because celestial movements are permanent.
D) Because time is an attribute of movement.

Key Takeaway
Time is the container of motion, not the motion itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If time is a container for your actions, are you filling it with what truly matters for your Hereafter? Which part of your day do you need to take back from its emptiness?
?
You say 'I will do that when...' but does your phrase treat time as a container or as an excuse? How would your schedule change if you saw time as a sacred vessel for obedience?
?
You move within time, but you do not own it. Every moment is a container given by Allah. What will you put in today's container that you will be ashamed to open on the Day of Reckoning?

Rational Judgments
intermediate
6 min
Time is Not an Attribute of Motion
Razi refutes that time is an attribute of motion and concludes his proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why time cannot be an attribute of celestial motion, and how Razi concludes that time is a distinct flowing entity.

Core Idea
Time cannot be an attribute of motion because then it would be both container and contained.

Razi now tackles the second possibility: that time is an attribute (ṣifa) of celestial motion. He argues this is even more absurd, because if time were an attribute, then motion would itself be a container for its own attribute, leading to the contradiction that one thing is both container and contained. He also provides additional supporting arguments to rule out any connection to motion, and finally concludes that time is a distinct flowing entity.

Guided Path
1
Understand the second possibility
Razi considers that the flowing thing might be an attribute of the celestial movement, such as speed or duration.
2
Follow the main argument
If time were an attribute of movement, then movement (which is the container of its attributes) would be contained in time, which is itself an attribute. This leads to the absurdity of one thing being both container and contained.
3
Examine additional evidence
Razi gives two more reasons: (a) if someone says 'God does an act when the planets stop moving,' that statement is not obviously false, but if time were motion, it would be absurd; (b) every attribute of motion is itself said to occur at some time, so time cannot be that attribute.
4
Reach the conclusion
All possibilities are eliminated except the third: time is a flowing entity distinct from both celestial motion and its attributes. That entity is what we call time (al-zamān).

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think time is the same as motion or its attribute.
Correction: Razi shows that time is a container for motion, so it cannot be the motion itself; and if it were an attribute, a contradiction arises.

Checkpoint
What is the main logical problem with saying that time is an attribute of celestial motion?
A) Attributes cannot be flowing.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Razi says that if time were an attribute of motion, then the statement 'God acts when the planets stop' would be obviously false. But you live your life as if your actions are only meaningful when you are moving—pursuing goals, making progress. When have you felt that stillness or waiting was 'wasted time'? If time is a real container independent of motion, what does that say about the value of your moments of stillness? Will you today embrace a period of stillness as fully contained in time, not empty but filled with presence?
?
Time is a flowing existent that is not the same as the events it contains. Your life is filled with events—prayers, work, conversations. Are you aware of the flow of time itself, or are you so absorbed in the events that you forget the container? If time flows independently, then every moment is a gift you cannot hold onto. What would change in your daily routine if you truly felt the passing of each moment as precious and irreversible?
?
Razi argues that every state of motion is located in time, so time cannot be a state of motion. Your own moods, thoughts, and actions all 'occur in time.' But do you ever feel that time is your own doing—that you control it by being busy? Reflect: are you using time, or is time using you? If time is a created, independent reality, how accountable are you for how you fill the container that Allah has given you? Today, decide one specific way you will honor time as a trust from Allah, not as a resource to be exploited.

Objection and Answer: Reinterpreting 'At the Rising of the Sun'
Objection and partial response regarding interpretation of temporal expression.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand an objection to a previous argument regarding temporal expressions and the beginning of Razi's response, which clarifies that concomitance does not eliminate the need for a temporal framework.

Core Idea
Reinterpreting 'at the rising' as 'with the rising' still implies a temporal relationship.

In this passage, Razi presents an objection that challenges the earlier interpretation of the phrase 'at the rising of the sun.' The objector suggests that the phrase merely indicates concomitance, not a definite time, thereby undermining the previous argument. Razi begins his response by pointing out that even the notions of concomitance and accompaniment themselves imply a connection that requires a temporal context. However, his response is cut off, leaving the full argument incomplete.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Understand the objector's two claims: reinterpreting the phrase and dismissing reliance on common speech.
The objector offers an alternative interpretation to avoid the earlier argument.
2
Identify the two parts of the objection
First, the objector reinterprets 'I will come to you at the rising of the sun' as 'I will come to you in a concomitant manner with the sunrise' or 'with the sunrise.' Second, he argues that the previous argument relies on common speech (ahl al-ʿurf), which is not reliable.
The objector tries to shift the meaning from a definite time to a mere relationship.
3
Examine the beginning of Razi's answer
Razi starts his answer by stating that 'that concomitance and accompaniment are not in essence (māhiyya) nor in...' The text cuts off, but the direction is to show that even these terms imply a temporal framework.
The answer is incomplete; only the first part is present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قيل : إنكم بنيتم هذا على أن المراد من قول القائل : آتيك عند طلوع الشمس ، هو أتيك في الوقت الذي تطلع فيه الشمس . ونحن لا نرضى بهذا التفسير ، بل نفسره بوجه آخر فنقول : المراد منه أتيك إتياناً مقارناً لطلوع الشمس ، أو مع طلوع الشمس . وعلى هذا التقدير فإنه يبطل ما ذكرتم . وأيضاً : فهذه الحجة مبنية على كلام يذكره أهل العرف ، ومثل هذا مما لا يلتفت إليه . والجواب عن الأول : إن تلك المقارنة والمعية ليست في الماهية ولا في
For it might be said: You have built this upon the interpretation that the speaker's statement 'I will come to you at the rising of the sun' means 'I will come to you at the time when the sun rises.' And we do not accept this interpretation; rather, we interpret it in another way and say: The intended meaning is 'I will come to you in a coming concomitant (muqārinan) to the sun's rising' or 'with the sun's rising.' On this assumption, what you have mentioned is invalid. Also, this argument is based on a statement mentioned by common people (ahl al-ʿurf), and such a thing is not to be relied upon. The answer to the first [objection]: That concomitance and accompaniment are not in essence (al-māhiyya) nor in...
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage presents an objection to the previous argument and the beginning of the author's response. The objector challenges the interpretation of the statement 'I will come to you at the rising of the sun.' The objector claims that the intended meaning is not 'I will come at the time when the sun rises' but rather 'I will come in a way that is concomitant with the sun's rising' or simply 'with the sun's rising.' Under this reinterpretation, there is no need to posit a distinct time as a container; the coming simply accompanies the rising. The objector also argues that the entire previous proof relies on a statement of common speech, which is not a reliable source for metaphysical arguments. The author's answer begins by addressing the first part of the objection. He states that 'that concomitance and accompaniment are not in essence (al-mahiyya) nor in...' but the text cuts off, leaving the answer incomplete. The beginning of the answer suggests that the notions of 'concomitance' (muqarana) and 'accompaniment' (ma'iyya) themselves imply a relationship that still requires a temporal framework, but the full argument is not present.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The phrase 'at the rising of the sun' can be interpreted as mere concomitance, eliminating the need for a temporal container.
Correction: Razi argues that even concomitance and accompaniment imply a relationship that still requires a temporal framework, as they are not inherent to the essence of the action.

Checkpoint
How does the objector reinterpret the statement 'I will come to you at the rising of the sun'?
A) As 'I will come to you at the time of sunrise.'
B) As 'I will come to you after the sunrise.'
C) As 'I will come to you with the sunrise' or 'concomitantly with it.'
D) As 'I will come to you if the sun rises.'

Key Takeaway
The objection attempts to reinterpret a temporal expression as mere concomitance, but Razi's response begins to show that even concomitance implies a temporal relationship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you use everyday phrases like 'at the time of prayer' or 'with the call to prayer,' do you unconsciously assume a temporal reality? How might your assumptions influence your understanding of Allah's relationship with time?
?
The objector here reinterprets words to avoid a conclusion. Have you ever redefined a term in your own beliefs to escape a difficult implication? What does that say about your commitment to truth?
?
Razi's response cuts off, but he implies that even 'accompaniment' is not in essence. How does your reliance on common language affect your understanding of metaphysical truths? Will you examine your own speech more critically?

The Proof of Time from Self-Evident Premises
The author answers the second question by linking debates to self-evident premises that necessitate time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how debates rely on self-evident premises and how this argument establishes the existence of time.

Core Idea
Debates are built on self-evident truths that inevitably imply time.

In this passage, the author addresses the second objection by grounding the debate in the very nature of rational discourse. He argues that all debates are composed of necessary sciences and depend on self-evident propositions. From this foundation, he shows that the concept of timing is unavoidable and leads directly to affirming the existence of time.

First Proof: Time Cannot Be a Measure of Celestial Motion
First proof against time as measure of celestial motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the first proof that time cannot be the measure of celestial motion, specifically the argument that motion's dependence on time is intrinsic to its nature.

Core Idea
Motion depends on time by its very essence, not by measure.

This lesson presents the first of several proofs against the Aristotelian view that time is the measure of celestial motion. The author begins by stating the thesis and then offers a proof that reduces the claim to a false dilemma. Understanding this proof requires careful attention to the nature of motion and its essential relationship to time.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the main claim
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice that the author first states the question and immediately declares the Aristotelian view false.
The proof is structured as a division (taqsim) into two alternatives.
2
Focus on the division into two alternatives
The proof divides the dependence of motion on time into two possibilities: either because of motion itself, or not. Both are declared false.
The author then explains why the first alternative is false.
3
Understand why the first alternative is false
The author argues that motion as such is defined by transition and requires succession of before and after, which only time provides. Hence motion inherently depends on time.
This shows dependence is essential, not accidental.
4
Grasp the conclusion
Since the ground of dependence (being motion) is common to all motions, time cannot be primarily a measure for some motions and derivative for others. Thus the measure concept collapses.
The proof ends here, but the implication is that time is not a measure but a prerequisite.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولنتكلم الآن في أن الزمان هل يعقل أن يكون مقداراً للحركة الفلكية كما هو قول أرسطاطاليس وأتباعه؟ فنقول: هذا المذهب عندنا باطل. ويدل عليه وجوه: الحجة الأولى: إن الحركة الفلكية الأولى، لما افتقرت إلى الزمان. فذلك الافتقار إما أن يكون لا لأجل كونها حركة، وإما أن يكون لأجل كونها حركة، والقسمان باطلان، فبطل القول يكون الزمان مقداراً للحركة. وإنما قلنا: إن القسم الأول باطل، لأن الحركة من حيث إنها حركة عبارة عن الانتقال من حال إلى حال. وإذا كان كذلك فالحركة من حيث إنها حركة لا تقرر ماهيتها، ولا تحصل حقيقتها، إلا عند حصول تعاقب القبليات والبعديات. وهذا المعنى لا يحصل إلا بسبب الزمان فثبت أن الحركة من حيث هي حركة مفتقرة إلى الزمان، وإذا ثبت هذا، فحينئذ لم يكن حصول الزمان لبعض الحركات ابتداء، وللباقي بالتبعية، أولى من العكس. لأن جهة الاقتضاء لما لم تكن إلا مجرد كونها حركة ثم إن هذا المعنى أمر مشترك فيه بين الكل على السوية، كانت جهة الاقتضاء حاصلة في الكل على السوية،
And let us now discuss whether time can be understood to be a measure of celestial motion, as is the statement of Aristotle and his followers? So we say: This doctrine is false according to us. And there are proofs indicating it: The first proof: The first celestial motion, since it depends on time. That dependence is either not because it is motion, or because it is motion, and both divisions are false, so the statement that time is a measure of motion becomes false. And we said: The first division is false, because motion in so far as it is motion is a transition from one state to another. And if that is so, motion in so far as it is motion does not have its essence determined nor its reality realized except when there occurs a succession of before and after. And this meaning does not occur except by means of time. So it is established that motion in so far as it is motion is dependent on time. And if this is established, then the occurrence of time for some motions originally and for the rest by consequence is not more appropriate than the opposite. Because the aspect of requirement, since it is nothing other than mere fact of being motion, and then this meaning is common to all equally, the aspect of requirement is present in all equally.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a proof (hujjah) against the Aristotelian view that time is the measure of celestial motion. The author first states the question: can time be understood as the measure of celestial motion as Aristotle and his followers claim? He then declares this doctrine false and introduces the first proof. The proof proceeds as follows: The first celestial motion depends on time. This dependence is either because of its being motion itself, or not because of its being motion. Both alternatives are declared false, so the claim that time is a measure of motion is invalid. The author then explains the falsity of the first alternative: motion, precisely as motion, is a transition from one state to another; its essence and reality are only realized through the succession of before and after, which occurs only through time. Therefore, motion as such is essentially dependent on time. From this it follows that it cannot be that time is primarily assigned to some motions and only secondarily to others, since the ground of dependence—being motion—is common to all motions equally. Hence the supposed measure-relation collapses: time is not a mere measure but a prerequisite for motion itself. The passage ends in the middle of this explanation, but the core argument is complete with the conclusion that both alternatives are false.

Duration Inheres in the Thing Itself
Author proves duration must inhere in the thing itself.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why duration must inhere in the thing itself and cannot be a separate entity, and how this relates to the definition of time as quantity of motion.

Core Idea
Duration is a modality of a thing's existence; it cannot exist apart from it.

This passage is a key philosophical clarification. The author refines the concept of duration, arguing that it is intrinsic to the thing that endures. He defines the quantity of motion as the extension of motion, and then shows that the extension of a thing's existence is its duration. By examining a dispute about whether permanence is an additional attribute, he proves that duration must inhere in the thing itself, not in something else. This reasoning underpins the definition of time as the quantity of motion.

Guided Path
1
Read the Passage
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its translation once through to get a sense of the argument's flow.
Pay attention to the author's initial statement of purpose.
2
Identify the Author's Purpose
The author starts by explaining his aim in quoting the Sheikh's speech: to show that his own proof is immune to the Sheikh's criticism, and then to point out a flaw in the Sheikh's argument.
This sets up the context for the subsequent definitions and proof.
3
Understand the Key Definitions
The author defines 'quantity of motion' as the extent (imtidad) of motion, and 'extension of existence' as permanence, continuation, and duration (dawam). These definitions are crucial for the proof.
Note that they are presented as conceptual truths.
4
Follow the Proof from Dispute
The author uses the historical dispute about whether permanence is an additional attribute to argue that duration must inhere in the thing itself. Even those who say it is additional hold that it inheres in the thing, not elsewhere.
The impossibility of duration being separate is presented as a necessary truth.
5
Appreciate the Conclusion
The conclusion is that the quantity of a thing's duration is a modality of that duration and must also inhere in the thing. Therefore, if time is quantity of motion, each motion has its own quantity; there cannot be a single time for multiple motions.
This directly impacts the definition of time.

واعلم أن غرضنا من نقل كلام الشيخ أن نبين : أنا إنما حررنا ذلك الدليل على وجه لا يتعلق به كلام الشيخ ولا يقدح فيه . ثم إنا بعد التنبيه على هذا المقصود ، نبين أن هذا الكلام الذي ذكره مختل من وجه آخر ، وتقريره : أن المعقول من مقدار الحركة [ هو مقدار امتداد الحركة (۱) ] لأنا إن لم نفسر مقدار الحركة بهذا المعنى ، لم يتلخص من قولنا : مقدار الحركة مفهوم ملخص معين ، وإذا عرفت هذا فنقول : [ المفهوم من امتداد وجود الشيء بقاؤه واستمراره ودوامه . إذا ثبت هذا فنقول (۲) : ] من المعلوم بالضرورة أن دوام وجود الشيء يمتنع أن يكون موجوداً مبايناً عنه ، حاصلا في غيره . وذلك لان الناس اختلفوا في أن بقاء الشيء واستمراره ، هل هو صفة زائدة على وجوده أم لا ؟ فمنهم من نفى كونه صفة زائدة، ومنهم من أثبتها . وكل من قال بذلك قال : إن تلك الصفة حاصلة في ذلك الشيء ، ويمتنع كونها حاصلة في شيء آخر ، وليس في العقلاء واحد يجوز أن يقول : إن دوام وجود الشيء لا يكون حاصلاً فيه بل في غيره ، وإذا ثبت أن دوام وجود الشيء يجب أن يكون فيه لا في غيره، فمقدار هذا الدوام لا معنى له إلا كيفية من كيفيات هذا الدوام فكانت هذه الكيفية ـ بامتناع المباينة - أولى . فثبت بما لخصناه : أنا متى فسرنا الزمان بمقدار الحركة (۳) كانت بديهة العقل حاكمة بأن مقدار كل حركة يجب أن يكون قائماً بتلك الحركة ، وأنه يمتنع أن يحصل هناك مقدار واحد يكون قائماً بواحد منها ، وتكون سائر الحركات في أنفها خالية عن مقاديرها .
Know that our purpose in quoting the speech of the Sheikh is to clarify that we only formulated that proof in a manner that the Sheikh's speech does not relate to nor refute it. Then, after drawing attention to this intended point, we show that this speech which he mentioned is defective from another aspect. Its exposition: that the intelligible from 'quantity of motion' [is the quantity of the extension of motion] because if we do not interpret 'quantity of motion' in this sense, our statement 'quantity of motion' would not yield a definite summary concept. And if you know this, we say: [the concept derived from the extension of a thing's existence is its permanence, continuation, and duration. If this is established, we say:] it is known by necessity that the duration of a thing's existence is impossible to be an entity separate from it, existing in something else. This is because people differed regarding whether a thing's permanence and continuation is an additional attribute over its existence or not. Some negated it being an additional attribute, and some affirmed it. And everyone who said that said that that attribute is inherent in that thing, and it is impossible for it to be inherent in something else, and there is no one among the rational people who would permit saying that the duration of a thing's existence is not inherent in it but in something else. And if it is established that the duration of a thing's existence must be in it and not in something else, then the quantity of this duration means nothing but a modality among the modalities of this duration. So this modality—due to the impossibility of separation—is more appropriate. So it is established by what we have summarized: that whenever we interpret time as the quantity of motion, the mind's intuition judges that the quantity of every motion must be subsisting in that motion, and that it is impossible for there to be a single quantity subsisting in one of them, while the other motions in themselves are devoid of their quantities.

Commentary
This passage is a clarification and a proof. The author states his purpose: to show that his formulation of the argument is immune to the sheikh's criticism, and then points out a flaw in the sheikh's own speech. He defines 'quantity of motion' as the extent of motion's extension (imtidad). He argues that the extension of a thing's existence is its duration, and that duration must inhere in the thing itself, not in something else. He analogizes to the dispute about whether permanence is an additional attribute; even those who say it is additional hold it inheres in the thing. Therefore, the quantity of duration is a modality of that duration and must also inhere in the thing. Thus, if time is the quantity of motion, each motion must have its own quantity, and there cannot be a single time for multiple motions.

Refutation of the Sheikh's Analogy
Author rejects the sheikh's body-measure analogy as sophistry.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the author argues that the sheikh's analogy between body measurement and time measurement is fallacious, and the implications for defining time as a measure of motion.

Core Idea
Each motion has its own quantity; a single time cannot measure different motions.

In this passage, the author directly refutes an analogy proposed by the sheikh regarding measurement. The sheikh had likened the measurement of bodies by a single quantity to the measurement of motions by a single time. The author argues that this analogy is a pure sophistry, because each body and each motion has its own intrinsic quantity, leading to multiple times if time is defined as the quantity of motion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Get a sense of the argument's flow.
The author uses a concise argumentative style.
2
Identify the sheikh's original analogy
Find the sheikh's statement: quantity in a body measures it and then measures other bodies. Understand how this analogy applies to time and motion.
3
Understand the author's refutation
Notice the author calls it 'pure sophistry' and gives a reason: each body has its own quantity, so by analogy each motion has its own quantity.
This is a direct disanalogy.
4
Recognize the absurd consequence
If time is the quantity of motion, then multiple motions would produce multiple times simultaneously. This is the 'aforementioned difficulties' returning.
The author uses reduction to absurdity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أما قول الشيخ : ( إن المقدار الموجود في جسم يقدره [ ثم تنقدر (4) ] سائر الأجسام بواسطته ، فنقول : هذا مغالطة محضة ، وذلك لأنه [ لما كان (۱) ] لكل كل واحد من تلك الأجسام مقدار على حدة ، فكذلك ههنا وجب أن يكون لكل واحد من هذه الحركات مقدار على حدة . وعلى هذا التقدير : إذا قلنا : الزمان عبارة عن مقدار الحركة ، لزم القطع بحصول الأزمنة الكثيرة دفعة واحدة ، وحينئذ تعود المحاولات المذكورة .
As for the Sheikh's statement: 'Indeed, the quantity existing in a body measures it, then other bodies are measured by means of it,' we say: This is pure sophistry. That is because [since] every single one of those bodies has its own quantity individually, so too here it is necessary for each one of these motions to have its own quantity individually. And on this basis: if we say that time is an expression for the quantity of motion, then it necessarily follows that multiple times occur simultaneously, and then the aforementioned difficulties return.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of an analogy presented by the sheikh. The sheikh argued that just as a quantity in one body can serve as a measure for other bodies, so too a single quantity of motion (time) could measure different motions. The author calls this a pure sophistry. He argues by analogy: just as each body has its own intrinsic quantity, each motion must have its own intrinsic quantity of motion. Therefore, if time is defined as the quantity of motion, each motion would have its own time, leading to multiple times existing simultaneously—an absurd consequence. This reinforces the earlier conclusion that time cannot be a single shared measure.

Key Terms

الأزمنة الكثيرة
المحاولات المذكورة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Time, as the quantity of motion, is a single measure that can be applied to all motions just as a single quantity measures all bodies.
Correction: Each motion has its own intrinsic quantity; therefore, if time is defined as the quantity of motion, each motion would have its own time, leading to multiple times simultaneously.

Key Takeaway
The sheikh's analogy between body measurement and time measurement is fallacious because each motion has its own quantity, so time cannot be a single shared measure.

Objection and Two Refutations on the Nature of Time
Objection and two refutations on time as necessitator of quantities.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the objection that time is a necessitator of quantities and the two refutations that defend the view that time is the quantity of motion.

Core Idea
The objector's attempt to separate time from motion leads to either self-contradiction or theological absurdity.

This passage presents a crucial objection to the preceding argument that time is nothing but the quantity of motion. The objector proposes that time is a separate entity that necessitates quantities of motion. The author provides two refutations: one exposing a contradiction in the objector's stance, and another showing that the objector's position would ultimately lead to identifying time with the Necessary Being (God), which is false.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and refutations once
Read the Arabic passage and translation without overanalyzing. Notice how the objector tries to redefine time as a separate necessitator.
2
Analyze the first refutation
The author points out a contradiction: the objector originally said time is quantity of motion, but now says it's a meaning that necessitates quantity. This is a shift in position.
The first refutation is about logical consistency.
3
Analyze the second refutation
The author argues that if time necessitates the duration of motion, and the duration of a contingent thing depends on its cause, then time would have to be the necessary existent (God). This is a theological reductio ad absurdum.
4
Summarize the lesson
The objection fails on two counts: internal contradiction and leading to an absurd theological conclusion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل : هذا الكلام إنما يلزم ، إذا قلنا : الزمان نفس مقدار الحركة ، ونحن لا نقول [ بذلك بل نقول إن (۲) ] لكل واحد من الحركات مقدار خاص بها على حدة . وههنا شيء آخر مباين عن الكل، هو المقتضى لحصول تلك المقادير ، وذلك الشيء هو الزمان . فنقول : هذا مدفوع من وجهين : الأول : إن مذهبكم أنه لا حقيقة للزمان إلا مقدار الحركة ، فلما أبطلنا عليكم هذا الكلام ، تركتم في هذا السؤال ، ذلك المذهب ، وقلتم : الزمان عبارة عن [ المعنى (۳) ] المقتضي لمقدار الحركة ، ومن المعلوم أنه فرق بين مقدار الحركة وبين المعنى المقتضي لمقدار الحركة. فإن قلتم : الزمان معنى يقتضي مقدار الحركة ، كان هذا تركا لقولكم : إن الزمان هو مقدار الحركة . والوجه الثاني في دفع هذا الكلام : هو أنا قلنا : إنه لا معنى لمقدار حركة الفلك ، إلا امتداد دوامها وامتدادها . ومعلوم (1) ] أن دوام الشيء الذي يكون ممكن الوجود لا يكون إلا لدوام علته الموجدة له ، فيلزمكم على قولكم أن تقولوا : إن الزمان عبارة عن الموجود الواجب لذاته الذي هو السبب الأول والعلة الأولى . وذلك باطل . والله أعلم
If a questioner says: 'This argument only follows if we say that time is the very quantity of motion, but we do not say that; rather we say that each one of the motions has its own quantity individually, and here there is something else separate from all of them, which is the necessitator for the occurrence of those quantities, and that thing is time.' We say: This is refuted from two aspects: First: That your doctrine is that there is no reality for time except the quantity of motion. When we invalidated this speech of yours, you abandoned, in this question, that doctrine, and you said: time is an expression for the meaning that necessitates the quantity of motion, and it is known that there is a difference between the quantity of motion and the meaning that necessitates the quantity of motion. For if you say: time is a meaning that necessitates the quantity of motion, this is an abandonment of your statement that time is the quantity of motion. The second aspect in refuting this speech: is that we said: there is no meaning for the quantity of the motion of the sphere except the extension of its duration and its extension. And it is known that the duration of a thing that is possible of existence is nothing other than through the duration of its efficient cause. So it follows from your statement that you would say that time is an expression for the necessary existence in itself, which is the First Cause and the First Agent. And that is false. And God knows best.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage presents an objection against the preceding argument. The objector tries to save the definition of time by distinguishing between time itself and the quantities of motion. He claims that time is not the quantity but something separate that causes those quantities to exist. The author gives two refutations. The first refutation points out that this contradicts the original position that time is nothing but the quantity of motion; now the objector is saying time is a meaning that necessitates the quantity, which is a different claim. The second refutation is theological: the quantity of the sphere's motion is nothing but the extension of its duration, and the duration of a contingent thing comes from its cause. Therefore, if time is what necessitates that duration, then time would have to be the self-necessary existent, i.e., God. But this is false and incompatible with the original view. Thus the objection fails.

المعنى

السبب الأول
العلة الأولى

Correction: Time is nothing but the quantity of motion; calling it a separate necessitator leads to contradiction or identifying it with God.

The view that time is an independent necessitator of motion quantities is self-contradictory and leads to the absurd conclusion that time is God.

The Fourth Proof: A Day Cannot Be an Attribute of Motion
Sanusi presents the fourth proof refuting time as a measure of motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the fourth proof against time as a measure of motion, which shows that a day cannot be an attribute of motion because that would involve the impossible self-subsistence of an attribute.

Core Idea
If a day were an attribute of motion, it would be an attribute in itself — which is impossible.

In this final proof against time as a measure of motion, the author presents a concise rational argument. He appeals to our intuitive knowledge that daily motion occurs within a day, and then shows that identifying the day as an attribute of motion leads to a contradiction. This reinforces the conclusion that time cannot be a measure of motion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the English translation. Let the wording sink in before analyzing.
Notice the concise, logical structure.
2
Identify the intuitive premise
The author states that every rational person knows intuitively that daily motion occurs with all its attributes in this day. This is the starting point of the proof.
Intuitive knowledge (بَدِيهَة) is a key concept.
3
Follow the conditional reasoning
If the day were an attribute of motion, then that attribute (the day) would be occurring in itself. This is an absurd self-reference.
This step reveals the contradiction.
4
Conclude the impossibility
Since something occurring in itself is impossible (بَاطِل مُحَال), the original assumption that the day is an attribute of motion must be false.
Thus time is not a measure of motion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الرابعة : إن كل عاقل يعلم بالبديهة أن الحركة اليومية، سواء كانت حركة فلكية أو عنصرية، فإنها إنما حصلت بذاتها وبجميع صفاتها في هذا اليوم، فلو كان هذا اليوم عبارة عن صفة من صفات بعض هذه الحركات، لكان ذلك حكماً بأن تلك الصفة حصلت في نفس تلك الصفة، وكان ذلك قولاً بحصول الشيء في نفسه، وأنه باطل محال.
The fourth proof: Every rational person knows intuitively that daily motion, whether celestial or elemental, occurs in itself and with all its attributes in this day. So if this day were an attribute of some of these motions, that would be a judgment that that attribute occurred in that same attribute, and that would be saying that something occurs in itself, and that is false, impossible.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a rational proof (burhan) that time cannot be a measure of motion. The author argues that we intuitively know that a daily motion (like a celestial sphere moving in a day) exists with all its attributes within that day. If the day itself were an attribute of the motion, then the day (as an attribute) would be occurring within itself, which is impossible (muhal). Therefore, the day is not an attribute of motion, so time is not a measure of motion.

Key Terms
الحركة اليومية
البديهة
الحصول في النفس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof is a general argument that nothing can be an attribute of itself, not specifically about time and motion.
Correction: The proof is specifically targeting the definition of time as a measure of motion. It shows that if time (the day) were an attribute of motion, an impossible self-reference occurs, so time cannot be a measure of motion.

Checkpoint

A) Time is a measure of motion
B) Time is not an attribute of motion because that would entail impossibility
C) Motion is eternal
D) The day is a substance

Key Takeaway
Time cannot be an attribute of motion because that would require an attribute to subsist in itself, which is rationally impossible.

?
If time is not an attribute of motion, then it is a separate created entity. How does that change your understanding of your own mortality and the moments you are given? Are you living each day as a gift from Allah, independent of the motions you perform?

The Fifth Proof: Time Exists Without Motion
The author presents the fifth proof with a conditional and two refutations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how conditional reasoning is used to prove that time is not the measure of motion.

Core Idea
Time is not the measure of motion; it persists even when all motion stops.

In this passage the author presents a sophisticated thought experiment: if time were merely a measure of motion, then without motion time would be impossible. Yet we can imagine a scenario with no motion and still perceive time's passage. This argument refutes the Aristotelian definition of time as 'the measure of motion'.

Guided Path
1
Understand the conditional argument structure
The argument begins with a conditional: if time were the measure of motion (antecedent), then without motion time would be impossible (consequent). The author shows the consequent is false, so the antecedent is also false.
This is a modus tollens argument.
2
Examine the first refutation: the thought experiment of stilling all motion
Imagine the heavens, sun, moon, and all planets are stationary, and even breath and glance are still. Yet we still perceive something passing like flowing water. This shows time exists without motion.
The perception of time is intuitive after reflection.
3
Examine the second refutation: the concept of 'afterness' without motion
Suppose the entire universe and its motions are annihilated. Their absence occurs after their existence. This 'afterness' implies time, even though motion is absent. The mind cannot avoid acknowledging time.
This argument uses temporal priority independent of motion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الخامسة : لو كان الزمان مقداراً للحركة، لكنا متى فرضنا عدم الحركة، وجب أن يتعذر علينا فرض وجود الزمان، لكن التالي باطل، فالمقدم مثله باطل. بيان الشرطية: أن فرض وجود مقدار الحركة، مع أنه لا وجود للحركة: محال في العقول. كما أن فرض وجود مقدار الجسم، مع أنه لا جسم: محال في العقول. وبيان بطلان التالي من وجهين: أحدهما: إنا إذا فرضنا كون الفلك والشمس والقمر وسائر الكواكب واقفة ساكنة وبالغنا في تسكين كل الحركات حتى النفس والطرف وغيرهما، فإنا نجد في صريح العقل وجود شيء يمر كالماء السيال، والعلم به ضروري بعد الاعتبار. وثانيهما: إنا إذا فرضنا عدم الفلك والشمس والقمر، وعدم حركاتها فلا بد وأن يقع عدمها بعد وجودها، وهذه البعدية بالزمان، فالذهن حال ما فرض عدم جميع الحركات، فإنه قد تعذر عليه الانفكاك من الاعتراف بوجود الزمان.
The fifth proof: If time were the measure of motion, then whenever we suppose the absence of motion, it would be impossible for us to suppose the existence of time. But the consequent is false, so the antecedent is likewise false. Explanation of the conditional: that supposing the existence of a measure of motion while there is no motion is intellectually impossible, just as supposing the existence of a measure of a body while there is no body is intellectually impossible. And explanation of the falsity of the consequent from two aspects: First: We explained that when we suppose the sphere, sun, moon, and all planets to be stationary and at rest, and we go to the extreme in making all motions still, even breath and glance and others, then we find in clear reason the existence of something passing like flowing water, and knowledge of it is necessary after reflection. Second: When we suppose the absence of the sphere, sun, moon, and their motions, then their absence must occur after their existence, and this 'afterness' is by time. So the mind, when supposing the absence of all motions, cannot avoid acknowledging the existence of time.
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage is a proof by conditional reasoning. The author sets up a conditional: if time were a measure of motion, then if no motion existed, time could not exist. But we can conceive of a scenario with no motion yet still perceive time (like flowing water), and even when we suppose the entire universe destroyed, we still recognize a temporal sequence of 'afterness'. Therefore the consequent is false, so the antecedent – that time is the measure of motion – is false. Two arguments are given to show the falsity of the consequent: the first is a thought experiment where all motions are stilled, yet we sense something passing; the second shows that the very concept of 'afterness' in the absence of everything implies time.

Key Terms
المقدار
الشرطية
البعدية الزمانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof requires that we actually make all motion stop physically.
Correction: It is a thought experiment; we only need to conceive of a scenario without motion to see that time is still perceived.

Checkpoint
What does the fifth proof aim to show?
A) That motion must exist for time to exist
B) That time can exist without motion, so it cannot be a measure of motion
C) That time is a substance
D) That motion is imaginary

Key Takeaway
Time is not a measure of motion because reason perceives its flow even in a motionless universe.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The mind cannot avoid acknowledging time even when all motion stops. What if your life's motion—your busyness, your striving—ceased right now? Would the time left have meaning? What are you filling your time with that will remain when all motion is gone?
?
You perceive time passing like flowing water. Every moment is slipping away. Are you living as if time is just a number, or as a reality that will hold you accountable? What will you change today to redeem the time you have?

The Sixth Proof: Time is Necessary in Itself
A proof that time is necessary in itself and not an attribute of motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that time is necessary in itself and why it cannot be an attribute of motion.

Core Idea
Time's necessity is proven because its non-existence leads to a contradiction.

This lesson presents a sophisticated rational argument that time must be necessary in itself. The author shows that if time were contingent, its non-existence would presuppose time itself, creating a contradiction. Then he demonstrates that time cannot be a property of motion, as that would imply motion is necessary. This argument uses the foundational concepts of wajib and mumkin.

Guided Path
1
Follow the proof for time's necessity
Read the first part of the passage carefully. The author begins by assuming time is not necessary, and then deduces a contradiction. Note how the concept of temporal afterness is used.
The argument hinges on the idea that non-existence after existence is a temporal relation.
2
Understand the contradiction
If time were not necessary, its non-existence would have to be after its existence, but that 'after' requires time to exist already. Hence assuming time's non-existence forces its existence, a contradiction.
3
Apply the rule: necessary in itself
The author concludes that anything with such a property (supposing its non-existence leads to contradiction) is necessary in itself. Time qualifies, so time is wajib al-wujud.
4
Examine the second argument: time cannot be an attribute of motion
Read the second part. If time were an attribute of motion, it would depend on motion, making it contingent. But time is necessary, so that's impossible. Also, the thing on which the necessary depends would itself be necessary, leading to motion being necessary—an absurdity.
This uses the principle that the dependent (mumkin) cannot be the independent (wajib).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة السادسة : الزمان واجب الوجود لذاته، وذلك يمنع من كونه متعلقاً بالحركة، ويمنع من كونه صفة من صفات الحركة. بيان الأول: أنه لو لم يكن واجب الوجود لذاته، لصح طريان العدم عليه، وكل ما صح عليه ذلك فإن بتقدير طريان العدم عليه، يكون عدمه بعد وجوده. وهذه البعدية، هي البعدية الزمانية. فثبت: أن الزمان موجود، يلزم من فرض عدمه، من حيث إنه هو: محال. وذلك لأن فرض عدمه يوجب فرض وجوده، وذلك يوجب الجمع بين النقيضين. وهو محال. وكل ما كان كذلك فهو واجب الوجود لذاته، ينتج: أن الزمان واجب الوجود لذاته. وإذا ثبت هذا فنقول: لو كان الزمان صفة للحركة، ومقداراً لها، لكان الزمان مفتقراً إلى الحركة، والمفتقر إلى الغير ممكن لذاته، فيلزم أن يكون الواجب لذاته، ممكناً لذاته. وذلك محال. وأيضاً: فالذي يفتقر إليه الواجب لذاته أولى أن يكون واجباً لذاته، فيلزم أن تكون الحركة واجبة الوجود لذاتها، فوجب كونها غنية عن المحل والموضع. وذلك محال.
The sixth proof: Time is necessary in itself, and that prevents it from being related to motion and from being an attribute of motion. Explanation of the first: If it were not necessary in itself, then non-existence could occur to it. And everything to which that is possible, when non-existence is supposed to occur to it, its non-existence is after its existence. And this 'afterness' is temporal afterness. So it is established that time exists such that supposing its non-existence, from the fact of its being itself, is impossible. That is because supposing its non-existence necessitates supposing its existence, and that necessitates combining two contradictories, which is impossible. And everything that is like that is necessary in itself. This yields: time is necessary in itself. And when this is established, we say: If time were an attribute of motion and its measure, then time would be dependent on motion, and what is dependent on another is possible in itself. So it would follow that what is necessary in itself would be possible in itself, and that is impossible. Also: That on which the necessary in itself depends is more fitting to be necessary in itself, so it would follow that motion is necessary in itself, and therefore it would be independent of substrate and location, which is impossible.
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a proof that time is necessary existence (wajib al-wujud li-dhatihi). The reasoning: if time could cease to exist, its non-existence would be after its existence, implying temporal succession, which requires time. So supposing time's non-existence leads to a contradiction (it must exist to conceive of its non-existence). Therefore time is necessary. Then, if time were an attribute of motion, it would be contingent (dependent on motion), contradicting its necessity. Also, if time depends on motion, motion would then be necessary, which is absurd. Hence time is not an attribute of motion.

Key Terms
واجب الوجود لذاته
الممكن لذاته
الجمع بين النقيضين
البعدية الزمانية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof treats time as a concrete independent entity like a substance.
Correction: The argument is conceptual: it shows that the very notion of time cannot be coherently thought of as non-existent, because any conception of its non-existence already presupposes time. It does not posit time as a concrete object.

Checkpoint
How does the sixth proof establish that time is necessary in itself?
A) By showing that time cannot be created
B) By arguing that supposing time's non-existence leads to a contradiction
C) By proving time is a substance
D) By relying on revelation

Key Takeaway
Time is proven to be necessary in itself because its non-existence leads to a contradiction, and it cannot be an attribute of motion because that would entail absurdities.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If time is necessary in itself, then every moment you experience is real and will be accounted for. Are you living as if each moment is a trivial illusion, or as a concrete reality that will confront you on the Day of Judgment?
?

?
This lesson forces you to recognize that time is not dependent on your movements—it is fixed. Are you using your limited time to seek what is necessary for your soul, or are you lost in contingent pursuits that will pass away?

Argument Against Time as a Composite of Nows
Al-Razi argues that past and future are nonexistent, so time cannot be composite.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Al-Razi's argument that time cannot be a real composite entity because past and future are nonexistent, and the present is an indivisible now.

Core Idea
Past and future are not real; only the indivisible now exists, so time is not a real composite.

Al-Razi presents a sharp critique of the philosophical notion of time as a real measure of motion. He invites us to examine what 'past' and 'future' actually refer to, and shows that they reduce to collections of present moments that no longer exist. This argument challenges the very foundation of considering time a real, continuous entity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once through, then read the literal translation. Notice the structure: a first result followed by a second point.
The Arabic begins with 'ينتج (١)' indicating a derived result.
2
Identify the two key claims
Distinguish between the first claim (past and future are nonexistent) and the second argument (if time were a measure of motion, it would be composed of successive nows, which is impossible).
The second claim builds on the first to show the impossibility.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
Understand that the conclusion is not just that time is unreal, but specifically that the measure of motion has no existence in external reality (fi al-a'yan).
This is a strong metaphysical claim about the status of time.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ينتج (١) : فلا شيء من الماضي والمستقبل بموجود الثاني : وهو أن الماضي هو الذي كان حاضراً ثم انقضى ، والمستقبل هو الذي يتوقع حضوره إلا أنه بعد لم يحضر ، لكن الحاضر ليس إلا الآن ، الذي لا يقبل القسمة ، فالماضي والمستقبل على هذا التقدير ليس إلا الآنات الحاضرة ، التي صارت ماضية، وذلك يوجب كون الزمان مركباً من الأنات المتتالية ، وهو عند القوم محال . فثبت : أن مقدار الحركة لو كان موجوداً ، لكان وجوده إما أن يحصل في الحال، أو في الماضي، أو في المستقبل . وثبت أن كل هذه الأقسام باطلة ، فوجب الجزم بأن مقدار امتداد الحركة لا وجود له في الأعيان البتة .
Result (1): Nothing of the past and future exists. Second: The past is what was present and then passed away, and the future is what is expected to come but has not yet come. However, the present is only the now, which is indivisible. So the past and future on this estimation are only the present nows that have become past. That necessitates that time is composed of successive nows, which is impossible according to the philosophers. So it is established that if the measure of motion existed, its existence would either occur in the present, the past, or the future. And it is established that all these divisions are false. So it is necessary to be certain that the extent of motion has no existence in external reality at all.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage presents an argument against the reality of time as an existent measure of motion. The author first states a result that nothing of the past and future is existent. Then he elaborates a second point: the past is what was once present and is gone, the future is anticipated but not yet present. The only real present is the indivisible 'now'. Therefore, past and future are merely collections of present nows that have become past, which would require time to be composed of successive nows—an impossibility according to the philosophers. The conclusion is that if the measure of motion (time) were existent, it would have to exist either in the present, past, or future. Since none of these are possible, the measure of motion has no external existence.

Key Terms
الزمان
الآن
الماضي
المستقبل
مقدار الحركة
الأعيان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Time is a real existing entity encompassing past, present, and future.
Correction: Al-Razi argues that past and future are not existent; only the present indivisible now has any reality. Therefore, time as a continuous real entity does not exist; the measure of motion has no external reality.

Checkpoint
What does the author conclude about the measure of motion?
A) It exists as a composite of nows
B) It has no existence in external reality
C) It exists in the past
D) It exists in the future

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi proves that the measure of motion (time) has no existence in external reality because it would have to be composed of nonexistent past and future moments.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If only the indivisible now truly exists, why do you spend so much mental energy dwelling on a past that no longer exists or worrying about a future that has not yet come? How can you train yourself to live more fully in the present moment, where you can actually obey Allah?
?
Al-Razi argues that the measure of your entire life has no external reality—it is just a succession of nows. Does this make you feel that your life is fleeting and insignificant in worldly terms? How should this affect your attachment to this world and your preparation for the eternal afterlife?
?
The philosophers considered time composed of nows to be impossible. If time as we experience it is not a real thing, what does that say about your perception of your own aging and mortality? Are you living as if your years are real possessions, or are you using each 'now' as a gift from Allah to draw closer to Him?

The Eleventh Proof: Time as Container Cannot Be an Attribute
Al-Razi argues that time, as a container, cannot be a property of motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's argument that time cannot be an attribute of motion because it is a container, and a container cannot be a property of what it contains.

Core Idea
A container cannot be a property of what it contains.

Al-Razi presents a concise proof based on self-evident axioms (badaha). He draws a distinction between a container and an attribute, arguing that time, which contains motion, cannot be a property of motion. This lesson unpacks that reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once silently, then read the literal translation. Notice how al-Razi uses two short syllogisms.
The passage is dense but clear.
2
Identify the premises and conclusion
Find the two premises: (1) time is a container for motion, (2) an attribute cannot be a container for its subject. Then see the conclusion that time is not an attribute of motion. Then identify the second line of reasoning about measure.
3
Reflect on key terms
Consider the terms 'zarf' (container), 'sifa' (attribute), and 'miqdar' (measure). How does al-Razi use them to build his argument?
These terms are foundational for understanding the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الحجة الحادية عشر : بدائه العقول شاهدة بأن الزمان ظرف للحركة ، وبدائه العقول شاهدة بأن صفة الشيء لا يكون ظرفاً للموصوف ، فوجب أن لا يكون الزمان صفة من صفات الحركة . ثم نقول : مقدار الشيء ، صفة من صفات ذلك الشيء ، ولا شيء من صفات الشيء زماناً لذلك الشيء ينتج : أنه لا شيء مما يكون مقداراً للشيء : زماناً له وذلك هو المطلوب .
The eleventh proof: The axioms of minds bear witness that time is a container (zarf) for motion, and the axioms of minds bear witness that the attribute of a thing cannot be a container for the described [thing]. Therefore, it is necessary that time is not an attribute of motion. Then we say: The measure of a thing is an attribute of that thing, and no attribute of a thing is a time for that thing. It follows that nothing that is a measure for a thing is a time for it. And that is what was required.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This brief proof argues from common sense (badaha) that time is a container for motion—motion occurs within time—and that a container cannot be an attribute (sifa) of the thing it contains. Since time is a container, it cannot be an attribute of motion. Furthermore, the measure of a thing is an attribute of that thing, but no attribute of a thing can be its time. Therefore, the measure of motion (i.e., time) cannot be time. The conclusion is that time is not the measure of motion.

Key Terms
ظرف
صفة
مقدار
بدائه العقول

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that because time measures motion, it must be a property of motion.
Correction: Al-Razi shows that a container cannot be a property of what it contains. Time contains motion, so it cannot be a property of motion.

Checkpoint

A) Because motion is not measurable
B) Because time is a container and a container cannot be an attribute
C) Because motion is eternal
D) Because time is not real

Key Takeaway
Time is a container for motion, and a container cannot be an attribute, so time is not an attribute of motion.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

If time is not a property of your actions, then your actions are not inherently 'long' or 'short' except by relation to the container. Examine your judgment of someone who spends 'little' time in prayer but does so with presence: is your judgment based on the container or the contained? How might this shift your understanding of sincerity?
?
The proof relies on self-evident axioms, yet you might still feel that time is intimately part of motion. Is your feeling an axiom or a habit? What assumption would you need to change to accept this distinction, and how might that change your perspective on the permanence of your deeds before Allah?

The Mind's Axiom: Conceivability as a Starting Point
Al-Razi opens his twelfth proof by asserting the conceivability of something, likely time without motion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Al-Razi uses the mind's intuitive recognition (بديهة العقل) to establish what is not impossible, and why this is a foundational move in kalam arguments about time and motion.

Core Idea
The mind's axiom tells us what is impossible—and what is not.

Al-Razi begins his twelfth argument by appealing to an axiom of the mind: something is not impossible to conceive. This brief opening is packed with methodological significance. In kalam, the rational faculty is trusted to deliver basic judgments about possibility and impossibility, forming the bedrock of theological proof. In this lesson, we will examine this single statement and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Read the fragment

2
Understand 'بديهة العقل'
بديهة العقل refers to intuitive, self-evident knowledge that the mind does not derive from reasoning. It is a starting point of rational argument.
This concept is central to kalam epistemology.
3
Ask what is being conceived
The text cuts off, but based on context, Al-Razi likely intended to say that the mind can conceive time without motion. Reflect on why this would be significant in debates about time.
4
Connect to kalam methodology
Notice how arguments in kalam often begin from what is rationally conceivable. This method establishes common ground before proceeding to proofs.

This passage is the beginning of the twelfth argument. The author states that it is not impossible for the mind to conceive something—likely the existence of time without motion.
